compactable blocks in the provided directory.\\n222: func (c *LeveledCompactor) Plan(dir string) ([]string, error) {\\n223: \\tdirs, err := blockDirs(dir)\\n224: \\tif err != nil {\\n225: \\t\\treturn \\n254: \\tres := c.selectOverlappingDirs(dms)\\n255: \\tif len(res) > 0 {\\n256: \\t\\treturn res, nil\\n257: \\t}\\n258: \\t// No overlapping blocks, do compaction the usual way.\\n259: \\t// We do having to care about data overlap.\\n261: \\tdms = dms[:len(dms)-1]\\n262: \\n263: \\tfor _, dm := range c.selectDirs(dms) {\\n264: \\t\\tres = append(res, dm.dir)\\n265: \\t}\\n266: \\tif len(res) > \\n289: // selectDirs returns the dir metas that should be compacted into a single new block.\\n290: // If only a single block range is configured, the result is always nil.\\n291: func (c *LeveledCompactor) selectDirs(ds []dirMeta) []dirMeta {\\n292: \\tif len(c.ranges) < 2 || len(ds) < 1 {\\n293: \\t\\treturn nil\\n294: \\t}\\n295: \\n296: \\thighTime := ds[len(ds)-1].meta.MinTime\\n297: \\n298: \\tfor _, iv := range c.ranges[1:] {\\n299: \\t\\tparts := splitByRange(ds, iv)\\n300: \\t\\tif len(parts) == 0 {\\n301: \\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n302: \\t\\t}\\n303: \\n304: \\tOuter:\\n305: \\t\\tfor _, p := range parts {\\n306: \\t\\t\\t// Do not select the range if it has a block whose compaction failed.\\n307: \\t\\t\\tfor _, dm := range p {\\n308: \\t\\t\\t\\tif dm.meta.Compaction.Failed {\\n309: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tcontinue Outer\\n310: \\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n311: \\t\\t\\t}\\n312: \\n313: \\t\\t\\tmint := p[0].meta.MinTime\\n314: \\t\\t\\tmaxt := p[len(p)-1].meta.MaxTime\\n315: \\t\\t\\t// Pick the range of blocks if it spans the full range (potentially with gaps)\\n316: \\t\\t\\t// or is before the most recent block.\\n317: \\t\\t\\t// This ensures we don't compact blocks prematurely when another one of the same\\n318: \\t\\t\\t// size still fits in the range.\\n319: \\t\\t\\tif (maxt-mint == iv || maxt <= highTime) && len(p) > 1 {\\n320: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn p\\n321: \\t\\t\\t}\\n322: \\t\\t}\\n323: \\t}\\n324: \\n325: \\treturn nil\\n326: }\\n327: \\n328: // selectOverlappingDirs returns all dirs with overlapping time ranges.\\n329: // It expects sorted input by mint and returns the overlapping dirs in the same order as received.\\n330: func (c *LeveledCompactor) selectOverlappingDirs(ds []dirMeta) []string {\\n331: \\tif !c.enableOverlappingCompaction {\\n332: \\t\\treturn nil\\n333: \\t}\\n334: \\tif len(ds) < 2 {\\n335: \\t\\treturn nil\\n336: \\t}\\n337: \\tvar overlappingDirs []string\\n338: \\tglobalMaxt := ds[0].meta.MaxTime\\n339: \\tfor i, d := range ds[1:] {\\n340: \\t\\tif d.meta.MinTime < globalMaxt {\\n341: \\t\\t\\tif len(overlappingDirs) == 0 { // When it is the first overlap, need to add the last one as well.\\n342: \\t\\t\\t\\toverlappingDirs = append(overlappingDirs, ds[i].dir)\\n343: \\t\\t\\t}\\n344: \\t\\t\\toverlappingDirs = append(overlappingDirs, d.dir)\\n345: \\t\\t} else if len(overlappingDirs) > 0 {\\n346: \\t\\t\\tbreak\\n347: \\t\\t}\\n348: \\t\\tif d.meta.MaxTime > globalMaxt {\\n349: \\t\\t\\tglobalMaxt = d.meta.MaxTime\\n350: \\t\\t}\\n351: \\t}\\n352: \\treturn overlappingDirs\\n353: }\\n354: \\n355: // splitByRange splits the directories by the time range. The range sequence starts at 0.\\n356: //\\n357: // For example, if we have blocks [0-10, 10-20, 50-60, 90-100] and the split range tr is 30\\n358: // it returns [0-10, 10-20], [50-60], [90-100].\\n359: func splitByRange(ds []dirMeta, tr int64) [][]dirMeta {\\n360: \\tvar splitDirs [][]dirMeta\\n361: \\n362: \\tfor i := 0; i < len(ds); {\\n363: \\t\\tvar (\\n364: \\t\\t\\tgroup []dirMeta\\n365: \\t\\t\\tt0    int64\\n366: \\t\\t\\tm     = ds[i].meta\\n367: \\t\\t)\\n368: \\t\\t// Compute start of aligned time range of size tr closest to the current block's start.\\n369: \\t\\tif m.MinTime >= 0 {\\n370: \\t\\t\\tt0 = tr * (m.MinTime / tr)\\n371: \\t\\t} else {\\n372: \\t\\t\\tt0 = tr * ((m.MinTime - tr + 1) / tr)\\n373: \\t\\t}\\n374: \\t\\t// Skip blocks that don't fall into the range. This can happen via mis-alignment or\\n375: \\t\\t// by being the multiple of the intended range.\\n376: \\t\\tif m.MaxTime > t0+tr {\\n377: \\t\\t\\ti++\\n378: \\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n379: \\t\\t}\\n380: \\n381: \\t\\t// Add all dirs to the current group that are within [t0, t0+tr].\\n382: \\t\\tfor ; i < len(ds); i++ {\\n383: \\t\\t\\t// Either the block falls into the next range or doesn't fit at all (checked above).\\n384: \\t\\t\\tif ds[i].meta.MaxTime > t0+tr {\\n385: \\t\\t\\t\\tbreak\\n386: \\t\\t\\t}\\n387: \\t\\t\\tgroup = append(group, ds[i])\\n388: \\t\\t}\\n389: \\n390: \\t\\tif len(group) > 0 {\\n391: \\t\\t\\tsplitDirs = append(splitDirs, group)\\n392: \\t\\t}\\n393: \\t}\\n394: \\n395: \\treturn splitDirs\\n396: }\\n397: \\n398: // CompactBlockMetas merges many block metas into one, combining it's source blocks together\\n399: // and adjusting compaction level. \\n254: \\tres := c.selectOverlappingDirs(dms)\\n255: \\tif len(res) > 0 {\\n256: \\t\\treturn res, nil\\n257: \\t}\\n258: \\t// No overlapping blocks, do compaction the usual way.\\n259: \\t// We do not include a recently created block with max(minTime), so the block which was just created from WAL.\\n260: \\t// This gives users a window of a full block size to piece-wise backup new data without having to care about data overlap.\\n261: \\tdms = dms[:len(dms)-1]\\n262: \\n263: \\tfor _, dm := range c.selectDirs(dms) {\\n264: \\t\\tres = append(res, dm.dir)\\n265: \\t}\\n266: \\tif len(res) > 0 {\\n267: \\t\\treturn res, nil\\n268: \\t}\\n269: \\n270: \\t// Compact any blocks with big enough time range that have >5% tombstones.\\n271: \\tfor i := len(dms) - 1; i >= 0; i-- {\\n272: \\t\\tmeta := dms[i].meta\\n273: \\t\\tif meta.MaxTime-meta.MinTime < c.ranges[len(c.ranges)/2] {\\n274: \\t\\t\\t// If the block is entirely deleted, then we don't care about the block being big enough.\\n275: \\t\\t\\t// TODO: This is assuming single tombstone is for distinct series, which might be no true.\\n276: \\t\\t\\tif meta.Stats.NumTombstones > 0 && meta.Stats.NumTombstones >= meta.Stats.NumSeries {\\n277: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn []string{dms[i].dir}, nil\\n278: \\t\\t\\t}\\n279: \\t\\t\\tbreak\\n280: \\t\\t}\\n281: \\t\\tif float64(meta.Stats.NumTombstones)/float64(meta.Stats.NumSeries+1) > 0.05 {\\n282: \\t\\t\\treturn []string{dms[i].dir}, nil\\n283: \\t\\t}\\n284: \\t}\\n285: \\n286: \\treturn nil, nil\\n287: }\\n288: \\n289: // selectDirs returns the dir metas that should be compacted into a single new block.\\n290: // If only a single block range is configured, the result is always nil.\\n291: func (c *LeveledCompactor) selectDirs(ds []dirMeta) []dirMeta {\\n292: \\tif len(c.ranges) < 2 || len(ds) < 1 {\\n293: \\t\\treturn nil\\n294: \\t}\\n295: \\n296: \\thighTime := ds[len(ds)-1].meta.MinTime\\n297: \\n298: \\tfor _, iv := range c.ranges[1:] {\\n299: \\t\\tparts := splitByRange(ds, iv)\\n300: \\t\\tif len(parts) == 0 {\\n301: \\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n302: \\t\\t}\\n303: \\n304: \\tOuter:\\n305: \\t\\tfor _, p := range parts {\\n306: \\t\\t\\t// Do not select the range if it has a block whose compaction failed.\\n307: \\t\\t\\tfor _, dm := range p {\\n308: \\t\\t\\t\\tif dm.meta.Compaction.Failed {\\n309: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tcontinue Outer\\n310: \\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n311: \\t\\t\\t}\\n312: \\n313: \\t\\t\\tmint := p[0].meta.MinTime\\n314: \\t\\t\\tmaxt := p[len(p)-1].meta.MaxTime\\n315: \\t\\t\\t// Pick the range of blocks if it spans the full range (potentially with gaps)\\n316: \\t\\t\\t// or is before the most recent block.\\n317: \\t\\t\\t// This ensures we don't compact blocks prematurely when another one of the same\\n318: \\t\\t\\t// size still fits in the range.\\n319: \\t\\t\\tif (maxt-mint == iv || maxt <= highTime) && len(p) > 1 {\\n320: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn p\\n321: \\t\\t\\t}\\n322: \\t\\t}\\n323: \\t}\\n324: \\n325: \\treturn nil\\n326: }\\n327: \\n328: // selectOverlappingDirs returns all dirs with overlapping time ranges.\\n329: // It expects sorted input by mint and returns the overlapping dirs in the same order as received.\\n330: func (c *LeveledCompactor) selectOverlappingDirs(ds []dirMeta) []string {\\n331: \\tif !c.enableOverlappingCompaction {\\n332: \\t\\treturn nil\\n333: \\t}\\n334: \\tif len(ds) < 2 {\\n335: \\t\\treturn nil\\n336: \\t}\\n337: \\tvar overlappingDirs []string\\n338: \\tglobalMaxt := ds[0].meta.MaxTime\\n339: \\tfor i, d := range ds[1:] {\\n340: \\t\\tif d.meta.MinTime < globalMaxt {\\n341: \\t\\t\\tif len(overlappingDirs) == 0 { // When it is the first overlap, need to add the last one as well.\\n342: \\t\\t\\t\\toverlappingDirs = append(overlappingDirs, ds[i].dir)\\n343: \\t\\t\\t}\\n344: \\t\\t\\toverlappingDirs = append(overlappingDirs, d.dir)\\n345: \\t\\t} else if len(overlappingDirs) > 0 {\\n346: \\t\\t\\tbreak\\n347: \\t\\t}\\n348: \\t\\tif d.meta.MaxTime > globalMaxt {\\n349: \\t\\t\\tglobalMaxt = d.meta.MaxTime\\n350: \\t\\t}\\n351: \\t}\\n352: \\treturn overlappingDirs\\n353: }\\n354: \\n355: // splitByRange splits the directories by the time range. The range sequence starts at 0.\\n356: //\\n357: // For example, if we have blocks [0-10, 10-20, 50-60, 90-100] and the split range tr is 30\\n358: // it returns [0-10, 10-20], [50-60], [90-100].\\n359: func splitByRange(ds []dirMeta, tr int64) [][]dirMeta {\\n360: \\tvar splitDirs [][]dirMeta\\n361: \\n362: \\tfor i := 0; i < len(ds); {\\n363: \\t\\tvar (\\n364: \\t\\t\\tgroup []dirMeta\\n365: \\t\\t\\tt0    int64\\n366: \\t\\t\\tm     = ds[i].meta\\n367: \\t\\t)\\n368: \\t\\t// Compute start of aligned time range of size tr closest to the current block's start.\\n369: \\t\\tif m.MinTime >= 0 {\\n370: \\t\\t\\tt0 = tr * (m.MinTime / tr)\\n371: \\t\\t} else {\\n372: \\t\\t\\tt0 = tr * ((m.MinTime - tr + 1) / tr)\\n373: \\t\\t}\\n374: \\t\\t// Skip blocks that don't fall into the range. This can happen via mis-alignment or\\n375: \\t\\t// by being the multiple of the intended range.\\n376: \\t\\tif m.MaxTime > t0+tr {\\n377: \\t\\t\\ti++\\n378: \\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n379: \\t\\t}\\n380: \\n381: \\t\\t// Add all dirs to the current group that are within [t0, t0+tr].\\n382: \\t\\tfor ; i < len(ds); i++ {\\n383: \\t\\t\\t// Either the block falls into the next range or doesn't fit at all (checked above).\\n384: \\t\\t\\tif ds[i].meta.MaxTime > t0+tr {\\n385: \\t\\t\\t\\tbreak\\n386: \\t\\t\\t}\\n387: \\t\\t\\tgroup = append(group, ds[i])\\n388: \\t\\t}\\n389: \\n390: \\t\\tif len(group) > 0 {\\n391: \\t\\t\\tsplitDirs = append(splitDirs, group)\\n392: \\t\\t}\\n393: \\t}\\n394: \\n395: \\treturn splitDirs\\n396: }\\n397: \\n398: // CompactBlockMetas merges many block metas into one, combining it's source blocks together\\n399: // and adjusting compaction level. Min/Max time of result block meta covers all input blocks.\\n400: func CompactBlockMetas(uid ulid.ULID, blocks ...*BlockMeta) *BlockMeta {\\n401: \\tres := &BlockMeta{\\n402: \\t\\tULID: uid,\\n403: \\t\\t}\\n422: \\t\\tres.Compaction.Parents = append(res.Compaction.Parents, BlockDesc{\\n423: \\t\\t\\tULID:    b.ULID,\\n424: \\t\\t\\tMinTime: b.MinTime,\\n425: \\t\\t\\tMaxTime: b.MaxTime,\\n426: c.plan(dms)\n240: }\n241: \n242: func (c *LeveledCompactor) plan(dms []dirMeta) ([]string, error) {\n243: \tslices.SortFunc(dms, func(a, b dirMeta) int {\n244: \t\tswitch {\n245: \t\tcase a.meta.MinTime < b.meta.MinTime:\n246: \t\t\treturn -1\n247: \t\tcase a.meta.MinTime > b.meta.MinTime:\n248: \t\t\treturn 1\n249: \t\tdefault:\n250: \t\t\treturn 0\n251: \t\t}\n252: \t})\n253: \n254: \tres := c.selectOverlappingDirs(dms)\n255: \tif len(res) > 0 {\n256: \t\treturn res, nil\n257: \t}\n258: \t// No overlapping blocks, do compaction the usual way.\n259: \t// We do not include a recently created block with max(minTime), so the block which was just created from WAL.\n260: \t// This gives users a window of a full block size to piece-wise backup new data without having to care about data overlap.\n261: \tdms = dms[:len(dms)-1]\n262: \n263: \tfor _, dm := range c.selectDirs(dms) {\n264: \t\tres = append(res, dm.dir)\n265: \t}\n266: \tif len(res) > 0 {\n267: \t\treturn res, nil\n268: \t}\n269: \n270: \t// Compact any blocks with big enough time range that have >5% tombstones.\n271: \tfor i := len(dms) - 1; i >= 0; i-- {\n272: \t\tmeta := dms[i].meta\n273: \t\tif meta.MaxTime-meta.MinTime < c.ranges[len(c.ranges)/2] {\n274: \t\t\t// If the block is entirely deleted, then we don't care about the block being big enough.\n275: \t\t\t// TODO: This is assuming single tombstone is for distinct series, which might be no true.\n276: \t\t\tif meta.Stats.NumTombstones > 0 && meta.Stats.NumTombstones >= meta.Stats.NumSeries {\n277: \t\t\t\treturn []string{dms[i].dir}, nil\n278: \t\t\t}\n279: \t\t\tbreak\n280: \t\t}\n281: \t\tif float64(meta.Stats.NumTombstones)/float64(meta.Stats.NumSeries+1) > 0.05 {\n282: \t\t\treturn []string{dms[i].dir}, nil\n283: \t\t}\n284: \t}\n285: \n286: \treturn nil, nil\n287: }\n288: \n289: // selectDirs returns the dir metas that should be compacted into a single new block.\n290: // If only a single block range is configured, the result is always nil.\n291: func (c *LeveledCompactor) selectDirs(ds []dirMeta) []dirMeta {\n292: \tif len(c.ranges) < 2 || len(ds) < 1 {\n293: \t\treturn nil\n294: \t}\n295: \n296: \thighTime := ds[len(ds)-1].meta.MinTime\n297: \n298: \tfor _, iv := range c.ranges[1:] {\n299: \t\tparts := splitByRange(ds, iv)\n300: \t\tif len(parts) == 0 {\n301: \t\t\tcontinue\n302: \t\t}\n303: \n304: \tOuter:\n305: \t\tfor _, p := range parts {\n306: \t\t\t// Do not select the range if it has a block whose compaction failed.\n307: \t\t\tfor _, dm := range p {\n308: \t\t\t\tif dm.meta.Compaction.Failed {\n309: \t\t\t\t\tcontinue Outer\n310: \t\t\t\t}\n311: \t\t\t}\n312: \n313: \t\t\tmint := p[0].meta.MinTime\n314: \t\t\tmaxt := p[len(p)-1].meta.MaxTime\n315: \t\t\t// Pick the range of blocks if it spans the full range (potentially with gaps)\n316: \t\t\t// or is before the most recent block.\n317: \t\t\t// This ensures we don't compact blocks prematurely when another one of the same\n318: \t\t\t// size still fits in the range.\n319: \t\t\tif (maxt-mint == iv || maxt <= highTime) && len(p) > 1 {\n320: \t\t\t\treturn p\n321: \t\t\t}\n322: \t\t}\n323: \t}\n324: \n325: \treturn nil\n326: }\n327: \n328: // selectOverlappingDirs returns all dirs with overlapping time ranges.\n329: // It expects sorted input by mint and returns the overlapping dirs in the same order as received.\n330: func (c *LeveledCompactor) selectOverlappingDirs(ds []dirMeta) []string {\n331: \tif !c.enableOverlappingCompaction {\n332: \t\treturn nil\n333: \t}\n334: \tif len(ds) < 2 {\n335: \t\treturn nil\n336: \t}\n337: \tvar overlappingDirs []string\n338: \tglobalMaxt := ds[0].meta.MaxTime\n339: \tfor i, d := range ds[1:] {\n340: \t\tif d.meta.MinTime < globalMaxt {\n341: \t\t\tif len(overlappingDirs) == 0 { // When it is the first overlap, need to add the last one as well.\n342: \t\t\t\toverlappingDirs = append(overlappingDirs, ds[i].dir)\n343: \t\t\t}\n344: \t\t\toverlappingDirs = append(overlappingDirs, d.dir)\n345: \t\t} else if len(overlappingDirs) > 0 {\n346: \t\t\tbreak\n347: \t\t}\n348: \t\tif d.meta.MaxTime > globalMaxt {\n349: \t\t\tglobalMaxt = d.meta.MaxTime\n350: \t\t}\n351: \t}\n352: \treturn overlappingDirs\n353: }\n354: \n355: // splitByRange splits the directories by the time range. The range sequence starts at 0.\n356: //\n357: // For example, if we have blocks [0-10, 10-20, 50-60, 90-100] and the split range tr is 30\n358: // it returns [0-10, 10-20], [50-60], [90-100].\n359: func splitByRange(ds []dirMeta, tr int64) [][]dirMeta {\n360: \tvar splitDirs [][]dirMeta\n361: \n362: \tfor i := 0; i < len(ds); {\n363: \t\tvar (\n364: \t\t\tgroup []dirMeta\n365: \t\t\tt0    int64\n366: \t\t\tm     = ds[i].meta\n367: \t\t)\n368: \t\t// Compute start of aligned time range of size tr closest to the current block's start.\n369: \t\tif m.MinTime >= 0 {\n370: \t\t\tt0 = tr * (m.MinTime / tr)\n371: \t\t} else {\n372: \t\t\tt0 = tr * ((m.MinTime - tr + 1) / tr)\n373: \t\t}\n374: \t\t// Skip blocks that don't fall into the range. This can happen via mis-alignment or\n375: \t\t// by being the multiple of the intended range.\n376: \t\tif m.MaxTime > t0+tr {\n377: \t\t\ti++\n378: \t\t\tcontinue\n379: \t\t}\n380: \n381: \t\t// Add all dirs to the current group that are within [t0, t0+tr].\n382: \t\tfor ; i < len(ds); i++ {\n383: \t\t\t// Either the block falls into the next range or doesn't fit at all (checked above).\n384: \t\t\tif ds[i].meta.MaxTime > t0+tr {\n385: \t\t\t\tbreak\n386: \t\t\t}\n387: \t\t\tgroup = append(group, ds[i])\n388: \t\t}\n389: \n390: \t\tif len(group) > 0 {\n391: \t\t\tsplitDirs = append(splitDirs, group)\n392: \t\t}\n393: \t}\n394: \n395: \treturn splitDirs\n396: }\n397: \n398: // CompactBlockMetas merges many block metas into one, combining it's source blocks together\n399: // and adjusting compaction level. Min/Max time of result block meta covers all input blocks.\n400: func CompactBlockMetas(uid ulid.ULID, blocks ...*BlockMeta) *BlockMeta {\n401: \tres := &BlockMeta{\n402: \t\tULID: uid,\n403: OOO disabled = oooTimeWindow is 0.\\n1037: // 1) Before: OOO disabled, Now: OOO enabled =>\\n1038: //   - A new WBL is created for the head block.\\n1039: //   - OOO compaction is enabled.\\n1040: //   - Overlapping queries are enabled.\\n1041: //\\n1042: // 2) Before: OOO enabled, Now: OOO enabled =>\\n1043: //   - Only the time window is updated.\\n1044: //\\n1045: // 3) Before: OOO enabled, Now: OOO disabled =>\\n1046: //   - Time Window set to 0. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01BDZ9f76sFmXwNrQpHv28Vs","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01996k7L5zZ59pvFhFsYaERW","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Prometheus TSDB Compaction Operational Runbook\n\n## 1. Overview\n\n### What is TSDB Compaction?\n\nTSDB compaction is a background process in Prometheus that merges overlapping time-series data blocks, removes deleted series (tombstones), and optimizes the database structure for efficient storage and querying. Compaction is essential for:\n\n- **Reducing disk usage** by merging blocks and consolidating tombstones\n- **Improving query performance** by maintaining reasonable block sizes\n- **Enabling storage retention** by building exponential block hierarchies\n- **Cleaning up WAL** by flushing persisted data from write-ahead logs\n\n### Block Structure and Compaction Levels\n\nPrometheus TSDB uses a **leveled compaction** strategy with exponential block ranges:\n\n- **Level 1**: Smallest blocks (default 2 hours) created directly from the head block\n- **Level 2**: Merged from 3+ Level 1 blocks (6 hours by default)\n- **Level 3**: Merged from 3+ Level 2 blocks (18 hours by default)\n- And so on...\n\nEach block is identified by a ULID (Universally Unique Lexicographically Sortable Identifier) in the format: `blocks/<ULID>/meta.json`\n\nBlock structure:\n```\n<ULID>/\n├── meta.json           # Block metadata, compaction level, stats\n├── index               # Series index file\n├── chunks/            # Compressed time-series data\n├── tombstones         # Deleted series markers\n└── .tmp-for-creation  # Transient directory during creation (atomic rename)\n```\n\n### Compaction Triggers\n\nCompaction is triggered by:\n\n1. **Time-based trigger** (primary): Runs every 1 minute (db.go:995), checking if head block is compactable\n2. **Head block compaction**: When head block time range exceeds `MinBlockDuration` (default 2 hours)\n3. **Explicit trigger**: Via `db.compactc` channel when appenders detect compactable data\n4. **OOO compaction**: When out-of-order samples accumulate in the head\n\nBlock selection for compaction follows rules in `compact.go`:\n- First, compact **overlapping blocks** (vertical compaction) if enabled\n- Then, select contiguous blocks matching exponential ranges\n- Finally, compact blocks with >5% tombstones regardless of size\n\n---\n\n## 2. Monitoring Indicators\n\n### Critical Metrics\n\n#### Compaction Activity\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total`** (Counter)\n  - Total compactions executed\n  - Healthy: Steadily increasing\n  - Alarm: No increase for >10 minutes with active writes\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_compactions_triggered_total`** (Counter)\n  - Total compaction attempts\n  - Healthy: Should exceed `compactions_total` (some are skipped)\n  - Warning: Triggered >> Executed (many failures)\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_compactions_failed_total`** (Counter)\n  - Failed compaction attempts\n  - Healthy: Should be 0 or very low\n  - **Red alert**: Any non-zero value indicates problems\n  - Note: Not incremented on context cancellation (shutdown)\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_compactions_skipped_total`** (Counter)\n  - Compactions skipped due to `--tsdb.auto-compaction-disabled`\n  - Normal when auto-compaction is disabled\n\n#### Compaction Performance\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds`** (Histogram)\n  - Time spent in compaction operations\n  - Healthy: p99 < 5 minutes, p99 < MinBlockDuration/2\n  - Warning: If duration approaches or exceeds `MinBlockDuration`, compactions are falling behind\n  - Critical: Log message at compact.go:1198 if duration > block time range\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_compaction_populating_block`** (Gauge, 0 or 1)\n  - Set to 1 during block writing, 0 when complete\n  - Healthy: Should be 0 most of the time\n  - Issue: Stuck at 1 indicates I/O problems or process hang\n\n#### Vertical Compaction (Overlapping Blocks)\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_vertical_compactions_total`** (Counter)\n  - Compactions of overlapping blocks\n  - Normal to increase if `EnableOverlappingCompaction=true`\n  - Indicates data arrived out-of-order\n\n#### Block and Storage Metrics\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_blocks_loaded`** (Gauge)\n  - Number of currently loaded blocks\n  - Healthy: Stable and not rapidly increasing\n  - Warning: Rapid growth suggests blocks are not being cleaned up\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_storage_blocks_bytes`** (Gauge)\n  - Total bytes used by all blocks\n  - Monitor against `prometheus_tsdb_retention_limit_bytes`\n  - If approaching limit, compaction may be blocked by retention\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_tombstone_cleanup_seconds`** (Histogram)\n  - Time to recompact blocks and remove tombstones\n  - High values indicate heavy delete operations\n\n#### Chunk Statistics (Level 1 Compactions Only)\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_compaction_chunk_size_bytes`**\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_compaction_chunk_samples`**\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_compaction_chunk_range_seconds`**\n\nThese indicate chunk quality; unusual distributions may suggest data quality issues.\n\n### Healthy Baseline\n\nFor a healthy Prometheus instance with 1-hour scrape of 10k series:\n\n```\nprometheus_tsdb_compactions_total: 50-100 per day\nprometheus_tsdb_compactions_triggered_total: 120-150 per day (some skipped/failed)\nprometheus_tsdb_compactions_failed_total: 0\nprometheus_tsdb_blocks_loaded: 30-50 blocks\nprometheus_tsdb_storage_blocks_bytes: 1-5 GiB (with default 15-day retention)\nprometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds: p99 < 2 minutes\n```\n\n### Alert Rules\n\n**PrometheusTSDBCompactionsFailing** (from prometheus-mixin):\n```\nincrease(prometheus_tsdb_compactions_failed_total{job=\"prometheus\"}[3h]) > 0\n```\n\nAdditional recommended alerts:\n\n```promql\n# Compaction falling behind\nincrease(prometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds_sum[5m]) /\n  increase(prometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds_count[5m]) > 300\n\n# Block accumulation\nincrease(prometheus_tsdb_blocks_loaded[30m]) > 5\n\n# Tombstone buildup\nprometheus_tsdb_blocks_loaded > 100\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. Failure Modes\n\n### Failure Mode 1: Disk Space Exhaustion During Compaction\n\n**Symptom:**\n- Compaction fails with error: \"no space left on device\"\n- Prometheus logs: `\"msg\"=\"compact blocks\" \"err\"=\"write block: ... : no such device\"`\n- Blocks stuck in `.tmp-for-creation` state\n- Metric: `prometheus_tsdb_compactions_failed_total` increments\n\n**Likely Cause:**\n- Insufficient disk space for compaction output (can require 2-3x the input block size during merge)\n- Retention limits not deleting old blocks\n- WAL not being truncated\n- Temporary block files not cleaned up from previous failed compactions\n\n**Diagnostic Steps:**\n\n1. Check disk usage:\n   ```bash\n   df -h /path/to/prometheus/data\n   ```\n\n2. Identify large blocks:\n   ```bash\n   du -sh /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/*/ | sort -h | tail -20\n   ```\n\n3. Check for orphaned tmp directories:\n   ```bash\n   find /path/to/prometheus/data -name \".tmp-for-*\" -type d\n   ls -la /path/to/prometheus/data/*.tmp/\n   ```\n\n4. Review retention settings:\n   ```bash\n   # Check configured retention\n   ps aux | grep prometheus | grep -E \"retention-size|storage.tsdb.retention\"\n   ```\n\n5. Check WAL size:\n   ```bash\n   du -sh /path/to/prometheus/data/wal/\n   ```\n\n6. Inspect Prometheus logs for which blocks failed:\n   ```bash\n   grep \"compact blocks\" prometheus.log | grep -i error | tail -20\n   ```\n\n**Code Reference:**\n- Compaction write: `tsdb/compact.go:606-717` (`LeveledCompactor.write()`)\n- Temporary directory cleanup: `tsdb/db.go:783-787`\n- Block deletion during failed compaction: `tsdb/compact.go:493-506`\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 2: Compaction Stuck or Not Progressing\n\n**Symptom:**\n- `prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total` and `prometheus_tsdb_compactions_triggered_total` stop increasing\n- `prometheus_tsdb_compaction_populating_block` stuck at 1\n- Query latency increases\n- Compaction duration increases steadily in logs\n- Blocks accumulate without being merged\n\n**Likely Cause:**\n- **I/O bottleneck**: Disk I/O saturation preventing block writes\n- **Memory pressure**: OOM killer or memory exhaustion preventing compaction progress\n- **Lock contention**: Compaction lock held by another operation\n- **Corrupted block**: Reading a corrupted source block blocks the entire compaction\n- **Slow disk**: NFS, storage array issues, or network-backed storage slowdowns\n- **Large blocks**: Attempting to compact excessively large blocks exceeds time/memory limits\n\n**Diagnostic Steps:**\n\n1. Check if Prometheus process is stuck:\n   ```bash\n   ps aux | grep prometheus\n   strace -p <pid> 2>&1 | head -20\n   ```\n\n2. Monitor system load and I/O:\n   ```bash\n   iostat -x 1 10\n   vmstat 1 10\n   top -p <prometheus_pid>\n   ```\n\n3. Check for OOM events:\n   ```bash\n   dmesg | grep -i \"oom\\|killed\\|memory\"\n   ```\n\n4. Examine compaction logs:\n   ```bash\n   tail -100 prometheus.log | grep -E \"compact|duration\"\n   ```\n\n5. Check block sizes:\n   ```bash\n   du -sh /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/*/ | sort -h | tail -5\n   # If largest block > 10GB, it may be too large to compact efficiently\n   ```\n\n6. Verify no blocks marked as failed:\n   ```bash\n   for block in /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/*/; do\n     grep -l '\"failed\":true' \"$block/meta.json\" 2>/dev/null && echo \"$block\"\n   done\n   ```\n\n**Code Reference:**\n- Compaction lock: `tsdb/db.go:1134` (`DB.cmtx`)\n- Duration warning: `tsdb/db.go:1197-1202` (logs if compaction exceeds `MinBlockDuration`)\n- Block population: `tsdb/compact.go:729-874` (`DefaultBlockPopulator.PopulateBlock()`)\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 3: Block Corruption\n\n**Symptom:**\n- Error on Prometheus startup: `\"corrupted block <ULID>: ...\"`\n- Index read errors: `\"open index reader for block ... : invalid checksum\"` or `\"corrupt index\"`\n- Query returns incomplete results from specific time ranges\n- Metric: `prometheus_tsdb_reloads_failures_total` increments\n- `prometheus_tsdb_blocks_loaded` drops suddenly\n\n**Likely Cause:**\n- **Incomplete block write**: Compaction crashed before fsync (especially on power loss)\n- **Metadata corruption**: Invalid `meta.json` or checksum mismatch\n- **Index file corruption**: Corruption in index file or chunks\n- **Filesystem inconsistency**: Unclean shutdown with corrupted filesystem\n- **Hardware failure**: Bit flip or disk sector error\n- **Unsafe snapshot**: Head chunks not properly re-encoded before compaction snapshot\n\n**Diagnostic Steps:**\n\n1. Identify corrupted blocks:\n   ```bash\n   # During startup, check Prometheus logs:\n   grep -i \"corrupted\" prometheus.log\n   ```\n\n2. Inspect block metadata:\n   ```bash\n   ls -la /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID>/\n   cat /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID>/meta.json | jq .\n   ```\n\n3. Check file integrity:\n   ```bash\n   cd /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID>/\n   # Verify required files exist\n   [ -f index ] && echo \"Index OK\" || echo \"MISSING: Index\"\n   [ -f chunks/000001 ] && echo \"Chunks OK\" || echo \"MISSING: Chunks\"\n   [ -f tombstones ] && echo \"Tombstones OK\" || echo \"MISSING: Tombstones\"\n   [ -f meta.json ] && echo \"Metadata OK\" || echo \"MISSING: Metadata\"\n   ```\n\n4. Check for incomplete creations:\n   ```bash\n   find /path/to/prometheus/data -name \".tmp-for-creation\" -type d\n   ```\n\n5. Validate block with promtool (if available):\n   ```bash\n   promtool tsdb check /path/to/prometheus/data\n   # or check individual block\n   promtool tsdb check /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID>/\n   ```\n\n**Code Reference:**\n- Block corruption detection on open: `tsdb/db.go:574-598` (`DBReadOnly.Blocks()`)\n- Meta file fsync: `tsdb/compact.go:702-703` (ensures metadata persisted)\n- WAL repair: `tsdb/db.go:918-933` (handles WAL corruption on startup)\n- Unsafe snapshot fix: `tsdb/compact.go:16` (CHANGELOG, re-encodes open chunks)\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 4: Out of Memory During Compaction\n\n**Symptom:**\n- Prometheus process killed by OOM killer: `dmesg | grep \"Killed process\"`\n- Compaction process exits without log message\n- `prometheus_tsdb_compactions_failed_total` increments (if processes restarts and detects failure)\n- Memory usage spikes during compaction before restart\n- Blocks may be left in `.tmp-for-creation` state\n\n**Likely Cause:**\n- **Large blocks being compacted**: Merging multiple large blocks (>5GB each) requires holding all data in memory\n- **High cardinality data**: Many unique series or labels increase in-memory symbol table\n- **Memory limit too low**: Container/pod memory limit insufficient for Prometheus + compaction\n- **Memory leaks**: Chunk pool not returning memory, builder allocations not freed\n- **Chunk pool exhaustion**: Too many chunks in flight, pool unable to recycle\n\n**Diagnostic Steps:**\n\n1. Check memory limit and usage:\n   ```bash\n   # Linux\n   free -h\n   cat /sys/fs/cgroup/memory.limit_in_bytes  # Cgroup limit\n   cat /sys/fs/cgroup/memory.usage_in_bytes  # Current usage\n   ```\n\n2. Monitor memory during compaction:\n   ```bash\n   watch -n 1 'ps aux | grep prometheus | grep -v grep'\n   # Note peak memory before OOM\n   ```\n\n3. Check for OOM events:\n   ```bash\n   dmesg | tail -30 | grep -i oom\n   docker logs <container> 2>&1 | grep -i oom  # For containers\n   ```\n\n4. Estimate block sizes:\n   ```bash\n   # If attempting to compact large blocks together:\n   du -sh /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/*/ | sort -h | tail -10\n   # Sum of largest blocks should fit in available memory\n   ```\n\n5. Check series cardinality:\n   ```bash\n   # Query Prometheus for cardinality (requires running instance)\n   curl -s http://localhost:9090/api/v1/label/__name__/values | jq 'length'\n   ```\n\n6. Inspect compaction plans:\n   ```bash\n   # Look at logs to see which blocks were selected for compaction\n   grep -E \"compact blocks|compaction plan\" prometheus.log | tail -20\n   ```\n\n**Code Reference:**\n- Block population allocates all data in memory: `tsdb/compact.go:729-874`\n- Symbol iteration: `tsdb/compact.go:803-810` (loads all symbols)\n- Chunk series merging: `tsdb/compact.go:812-823` (memory-intensive for large series sets)\n- Chunk pool exhaustion: `tsdb/compact.go:863-867` (returns chunks to pool)\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 5: WAL Corruption or Loss\n\n**Symptom:**\n- Prometheus startup error: `\"read WAL: ... error\" or \"read wal: ...\" or \"corrupted WAL\"`\n- Samples missing after a crash\n- Metric: `prometheus_tsdb_wal_reader_corruption_errors_total` increments\n- Compaction cannot complete (head block cannot persist)\n- `prometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds_count` stops increasing\n\n**Likely Cause:**\n- **Unclean shutdown**: Process killed or power loss during WAL write\n- **Corrupted WAL segment**: Disk error or incomplete write\n- **Disk full**: WAL write failed halfway through\n- **File system issue**: Metadata corruption or inode issues\n- **Concurrent WAL access**: Multiple instances writing to same TSDB directory\n\n**Diagnostic Steps:**\n\n1. Check WAL directory:\n   ```bash\n   ls -lh /path/to/prometheus/data/wal/\n   ```\n\n2. Check WAL segment integrity:\n   ```bash\n   # Prometheus will attempt to repair on startup; check logs:\n   grep -E \"WAL|wal\" prometheus.log | grep -i \"repair\\|error\" | head -20\n   ```\n\n3. Verify WAL repair status:\n   ```bash\n   grep \"Successfully repaired WAL\" prometheus.log  # Good sign\n   grep \"repair corrupted WAL\" prometheus.log       # Repair attempted\n   ```\n\n4. Check for WBL (write-behind log for out-of-order data):\n   ```bash\n   ls -lh /path/to/prometheus/data/wbl/ 2>/dev/null || echo \"No WBL\"\n   ```\n\n5. Monitor disk I/O during startup:\n   ```bash\n   # During restart, check:\n   iostat -x 1 | grep -E \"rrqm|wrqm|util\"\n   ```\n\n**Code Reference:**\n- WAL repair on startup: `tsdb/db.go:918-933` (automatic repair)\n- WAL truncation: `tsdb/db.go:1147-1150` (happens after successful compaction)\n- WBL (write-behind log) for OOO: `tsdb/db.go:858-863` (separate log for out-of-order samples)\n\n---\n\n## 4. Recovery Procedures\n\n### Procedure 1: Recover from Disk Space Exhaustion\n\n**Prerequisites:**\n- SSH/physical access to Prometheus instance\n- Sufficient disk space to add at least 10% more capacity or free up space\n\n**Steps:**\n\n1. **Stop Prometheus gracefully:**\n   ```bash\n   # Signal process to gracefully shutdown (gives it time to close files)\n   kill -TERM <prometheus_pid>\n   # Wait up to 30 seconds for graceful shutdown\n   sleep 30\n   if ps -p <prometheus_pid> > /dev/null; then\n     kill -9 <prometheus_pid>  # Force kill if still running\n   fi\n   ```\n\n2. **Clean up temporary block directories:**\n   ```bash\n   # Remove incomplete block creations (safe to delete)\n   find /path/to/prometheus/data -name \".tmp-for-*\" -type d -exec rm -rf {} + 2>/dev/null || true\n   ls -la /path/to/prometheus/data/*.tmp 2>/dev/null | xargs rm -rf || true\n   ```\n\n3. **Check WAL truncation:**\n   ```bash\n   # WAL can be large; compress if needed\n   du -sh /path/to/prometheus/data/wal/\n   # Note: Don't delete WAL; let Prometheus handle it on restart\n   ```\n\n4. **Verify block consistency:**\n   ```bash\n   # List all blocks\n   ls /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/\n\n   # Check for blocks with failed compaction flag\n   for block in /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/*/; do\n     if grep -q '\"failed\":true' \"$block/meta.json\" 2>/dev/null; then\n       echo \"Failed block: $block\"\n     fi\n   done\n   ```\n\n5. **Optional: Delete oldest blocks if still out of space**\n   ```bash\n   # Only if disk is still critically low\n   # List blocks by date (ULID timestamp)\n   ls -la /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/ | sort -k6\n\n   # Delete oldest 2-3 blocks (they're the smallest)\n   # WARNING: This loses data outside retention!\n   rm -rf /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<oldest_ULID>\n   ```\n\n6. **Restart Prometheus:**\n   ```bash\n   # Restart with monitoring\n   systemctl start prometheus  # or docker run, kubectl apply, etc.\n\n   # Verify startup\n   sleep 10\n   curl -s http://localhost:9090/-/healthy\n   ```\n\n7. **Monitor recovery:**\n   ```bash\n   # Watch for compaction to resume\n   watch 'curl -s http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total | jq'\n\n   # Check error logs\n   tail -f prometheus.log | grep -E \"compact|error|warn\"\n   ```\n\n8. **Verify disk recovery:**\n   ```bash\n   # After 30 minutes, check if disk usage decreasing\n   watch -n 60 'du -sh /path/to/prometheus/data; df -h /path/to/prometheus/data'\n   ```\n\n**Expected Outcome:**\n- `prometheus_tsdb_compactions_failed_total` stays stable (no new failures)\n- `prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total` resumes increasing\n- Disk usage stabilizes and then decreases as old blocks are deleted by retention\n\n---\n\n### Procedure 2: Recover from Stuck Compaction\n\n**Prerequisites:**\n- Prometheus instance is running but compaction not progressing\n- At least 5 minutes of observation confirming no progress\n\n**Steps:**\n\n1. **Verify compaction is truly stuck:**\n   ```bash\n   # Check if compaction counter increasing\n   curl -s http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=rate(prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total[5m]) | jq '.data.result[0].value[1]'\n   # Should be > 0 if healthy\n\n   # If query returns \"null\" or \"0\", compaction is likely stuck\n   ```\n\n2. **Check system resources:**\n   ```bash\n   # CPU usage\n   top -p <prometheus_pid> -b -n 1 | tail -5\n\n   # Disk I/O\n   iostat -x 1 5 | tail -10\n\n   # Memory\n   ps aux | grep prometheus | grep -v grep | awk '{print $6 \" KB\"}'\n   ```\n\n3. **Identify the blocked block:**\n   ```bash\n   # Find what compaction is processing\n   lsof -p <prometheus_pid> | grep /blocks/ | head -10\n   # Look for which block directory is open\n\n   # Check metadata of candidates\n   for block in /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/*/; do\n     size=$(du -sh \"$block\" | cut -f1)\n     echo \"$block: $size\"\n   done | sort -h -k3 | tail -5\n   ```\n\n4. **Check logs for last compaction attempt:**\n   ```bash\n   tail -200 prometheus.log | grep -E \"compact|error|duration\" | tail -20\n   ```\n\n5. **Gracefully restart Prometheus:**\n   ```bash\n   # Trigger graceful shutdown\n   systemctl stop prometheus  # or equivalent\n\n   # Wait for shutdown\n   sleep 30\n   ```\n\n6. **Check for corrupted source block:**\n   ```bash\n   # If blocks are suspected corrupted, validate with promtool\n   promtool tsdb check /path/to/prometheus/data 2>&1 | head -50\n   # Look for \"corrupted\" errors\n   ```\n\n7. **Restart Prometheus:**\n   ```bash\n   systemctl start prometheus\n   sleep 15\n   curl -s http://localhost:9090/-/healthy\n   ```\n\n8. **Monitor for issue recurrence:**\n   ```bash\n   # Watch compaction duration\n   watch -n 10 'curl -s \"http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=rate(prometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds_sum[5m])/rate(prometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds_count[5m])\" | jq \".data.result[0].value[1]\" 2>/dev/null || echo \"unavailable\"'\n\n   # Should see compactions resuming within 1-2 minutes\n   ```\n\n**Expected Outcome:**\n- `prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total` resumes increasing after restart\n- Compaction duration returns to normal (<5 minutes)\n- No \"stuck\" symptoms after 10 minutes of monitoring\n\n---\n\n### Procedure 3: Recover from Block Corruption\n\n**Prerequisites:**\n- Prometheus cannot start or logs show `\"corrupted block\"` error\n- Identify the corrupted block ULID from logs\n\n**Steps:**\n\n1. **Identify corrupted blocks:**\n   ```bash\n   # Try to start Prometheus and capture error\n   prometheus --config.file=/etc/prometheus/prometheus.yml 2>&1 | grep -i \"corrupted\"\n   # Note the ULID in the error\n\n   # Or check all blocks:\n   for block in /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/*/; do\n     if ! promtool tsdb check \"$block\" &>/dev/null; then\n       echo \"Corrupted: $block\"\n     fi\n   done\n   ```\n\n2. **Determine block importance:**\n   ```bash\n   # Get block time range\n   cat /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID>/meta.json | jq '{minTime: .minTime, maxTime: .maxTime}'\n\n   # Convert timestamps (milliseconds since epoch)\n   python3 -c \"import datetime; print(datetime.datetime.fromtimestamp(1234567890 / 1000))\"\n   ```\n\n3. **Check if block has children (i.e., was compacted):**\n   ```bash\n   # If this block is parent of others, don't delete it\n   grep -r '<ULID>' /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/*/meta.json | grep \"sources\" | head -10\n   # If no results, block is safe to delete\n   ```\n\n4. **Option A: Delete corrupted block (data loss for time range)**\n   ```bash\n   # This is safe if block has been replaced by newer compacted blocks\n   rm -rf /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID>\n\n   # Verify deletion\n   ls /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID> 2>/dev/null || echo \"Block deleted\"\n   ```\n\n5. **Option B: Attempt repair with promtool (experimental)**\n   ```bash\n   # First backup the block\n   cp -r /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID> /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID>.backup\n\n   # Attempt repair (not always successful)\n   promtool tsdb repair /path/to/prometheus/data 2>&1\n\n   # Check if fixed\n   promtool tsdb check /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID> 2>&1\n   ```\n\n6. **Restart Prometheus:**\n   ```bash\n   prometheus --config.file=/etc/prometheus/prometheus.yml &\n   sleep 10\n   curl -s http://localhost:9090/-/healthy\n   ```\n\n7. **Verify recovery:**\n   ```bash\n   # Check that Prometheus is queryable\n   curl -s 'http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=up' | jq '.status'\n   # Should return \"success\"\n\n   # Verify block loading\n   curl -s 'http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=prometheus_tsdb_blocks_loaded' | jq '.data.result[0].value[1]'\n   ```\n\n**Expected Outcome:**\n- Prometheus starts without corruption errors\n- Metrics queryable from remaining blocks\n- Data loss limited to corrupted block's time range\n\n**Note:** If multiple blocks are corrupted, consider full database rebuild from backups.\n\n---\n\n### Procedure 4: Recover from OOM During Compaction\n\n**Prerequisites:**\n- Prometheus was killed by OOM killer\n- Available memory or pod memory limit can be increased\n- Database backups available (optional but recommended)\n\n**Steps:**\n\n1. **Verify OOM occurred:**\n   ```bash\n   dmesg | tail -20 | grep -i \"oom\\|killed\"\n   # Should show: \"Killed process <pid> (prometheus)\"\n   ```\n\n2. **Increase memory limit (if container/pod):**\n   ```bash\n   # Docker\n   docker update --memory 8g <container_id>\n\n   # Kubernetes\n   kubectl set resources deployment prometheus --limits=memory=8G\n\n   # Systemd service: edit /etc/systemd/system/prometheus.service\n   # Add: MemoryLimit=8G\n   systemctl daemon-reload\n   ```\n\n3. **Clean up incomplete blocks:**\n   ```bash\n   # Remove temporary block creations\n   find /path/to/prometheus/data -name \".tmp-for-*\" -type d -exec rm -rf {} + 2>/dev/null || true\n   ```\n\n4. **Reduce block compaction size (optional, advanced):**\n   ```bash\n   # Edit Prometheus config to use smaller blocks\n   # This prevents very large merges that cause OOM\n\n   # Add to prometheus.yml (restart required):\n   # storage:\n   #   tsdb:\n   #     min-block-duration: 1h\n   #     max-block-duration: 1h  # Prevent large merges\n   ```\n\n5. **Restart Prometheus:**\n   ```bash\n   systemctl start prometheus\n   # or docker run with new memory limit\n   docker run --memory 8g ... prometheus\n\n   sleep 15\n   curl -s http://localhost:9090/-/healthy\n   ```\n\n6. **Monitor memory and compaction:**\n   ```bash\n   # Watch memory during first compaction\n   watch -n 5 'ps aux | grep prometheus | grep -v grep | awk \"{print \\$6 \\\" KB\\\"}\"'\n\n   # In another terminal, monitor compaction\n   watch -n 5 'curl -s \"http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total\" | jq \".data.result[0].value[1]\" 2>/dev/null || echo \"loading\"'\n   ```\n\n7. **Verify stable operation:**\n   ```bash\n   # After 1 hour of operation, check for OOM recurrence\n   dmesg | tail -10 | grep -i \"oom\" || echo \"No new OOM events\"\n\n   # Check compaction metrics\n   curl -s 'http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=prometheus_tsdb_compactions_failed_total' | jq '.data.result[0].value[1]'\n   # Should be \"0\"\n   ```\n\n**Expected Outcome:**\n- Prometheus runs without OOM restarts\n- Memory usage stabilizes below limit during compaction\n- Compactions complete successfully\n\n**Long-term mitigation:**\n- Reduce series cardinality (drop unnecessary labels/series)\n- Increase retention interval or use size-based retention\n- Use query optimization to reduce query memory footprint\n\n---\n\n### Procedure 5: Recover from WAL Corruption\n\n**Prerequisites:**\n- Prometheus fails to start with WAL errors\n- WAL corruption is unrecoverable or too severe to repair\n\n**Steps:**\n\n1. **Verify WAL is the issue:**\n   ```bash\n   # Try to start Prometheus\n   prometheus --config.file=/etc/prometheus/prometheus.yml 2>&1 | grep -i \"wal\\|wbl\"\n\n   # Should see error like:\n   # \"Encountered WAL read error, attempting repair\"\n   # \"repair corrupted WAL: ...\"\n   ```\n\n2. **Let Prometheus attempt auto-repair:**\n   ```bash\n   # The code in tsdb/db.go:918-933 automatically repairs WAL\n   # Just restart Prometheus; it will try to fix issues\n   prometheus --config.file=/etc/prometheus/prometheus.yml &\n   sleep 30\n   jobs\n   # If process is running, repair succeeded\n   ```\n\n3. **Check repair status:**\n   ```bash\n   # Look for success message\n   grep \"Successfully repaired\" prometheus.log\n   # If found, WAL was fixed; Prometheus should be running\n\n   curl -s http://localhost:9090/-/healthy\n   ```\n\n4. **If auto-repair fails, manually reset WAL:**\n   ```bash\n   # WARNING: This loses data in the WAL (typically <2 hours of data)\n\n   # Stop Prometheus\n   kill -9 <prometheus_pid>\n\n   # Backup corrupted WAL\n   mv /path/to/prometheus/data/wal /path/to/prometheus/data/wal.corrupted\n   mkdir -p /path/to/prometheus/data/wal\n\n   # Backup WBL (write-behind log) if it exists\n   if [ -d /path/to/prometheus/data/wbl ]; then\n     mv /path/to/prometheus/data/wbl /path/to/prometheus/data/wbl.corrupted\n   fi\n   ```\n\n5. **Restart Prometheus with empty WAL:**\n   ```bash\n   prometheus --config.file=/etc/prometheus/prometheus.yml &\n   sleep 10\n   curl -s http://localhost:9090/-/healthy\n\n   # Should be running with new WAL\n   ls -la /path/to/prometheus/data/wal/\n   ```\n\n6. **Verify data recovery:**\n   ```bash\n   # Check how much data was lost\n   curl -s 'http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=prometheus_tsdb_blocks_loaded' | jq '.data.result[0].value[1]'\n   # Should still show blocks from persisted storage\n\n   # Query for time range to see what data remains\n   curl -s 'http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query_range?query=up&start=...&end=...&step=...' | jq '.data'\n   ```\n\n7. **Monitor compaction after WAL reset:**\n   ```bash\n   # New compaction may be triggered to persist head data\n   tail -f prometheus.log | grep -E \"compact|wal\"\n\n   # Check that compactions complete successfully\n   watch -n 30 'curl -s http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=rate(prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total[5m]) | jq \".data.result[0].value[1]\"'\n   ```\n\n**Expected Outcome:**\n- Prometheus starts and serves queries\n- Data loss limited to samples in lost WAL (typically < 2 hours)\n- Blocks on disk are preserved\n- New WAL created for future samples\n\n**Note:** If WAL corruption is recurring, check for hardware issues (disk errors, memory corruption) or filesystem problems.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Overview\n\n### What is TSDB Compaction?\n\nTSDB compaction is a background process in Prometheus that merges overlapping time-series data blocks, removes deleted series (tombstones), and optimizes the database structure for efficient storage and querying. Compaction is essential for:\n\n- **Reducing disk usage** by merging blocks and consolidating tombstones\n- **Improving query performance** by maintaining reasonable block sizes\n- **Enabling storage retention** by building exponential block hierarchies\n- **Cleaning up WAL** by flushing persisted data from write-ahead logs\n\n### Block Structure and Compaction Levels\n\nPrometheus TSDB uses a **leveled compaction** strategy with exponential block ranges:\n\n- **Level 1**: Smallest blocks (default 2 hours) created directly from the head block\n- **Level 2**: Merged from 3+ Level 1 blocks (6 hours by default)\n- **Level 3**: Merged from 3+ Level 2 blocks (18 hours by default)\n- And so on...\n\nEach block is identified by a ULID (Universally Unique Lexicographically Sortable Identifier) in the format: `blocks/<ULID>/meta.json`\n\nBlock structure:\n```\n<ULID>/\n├── meta.json           # Block metadata, compaction level, stats\n├── index               # Series index file\n├── chunks/            # Compressed time-series data\n├── tombstones         # Deleted series markers\n└── .tmp-for-creation  # Transient directory during creation (atomic rename)\n```\n\n### Compaction Triggers\n\nCompaction is triggered by:\n\n1. **Time-based trigger** (primary): Runs every 1 minute (db.go:995), checking if head block is compactable\n2. **Head block compaction**: When head block time range exceeds `MinBlockDuration` (default 2 hours)\n3. **Explicit trigger**: Via `db.compactc` channel when appenders detect compactable data\n4. **OOO compaction**: When out-of-order samples accumulate in the head\n\nBlock selection for compaction follows rules in `compact.go`:\n- First, compact **overlapping blocks** (vertical compaction) if enabled\n- Then, select contiguous blocks matching exponential ranges\n- Finally, compact blocks with >5% tombstones regardless of size\n\n---\n\n## 2. Monitoring Indicators\n\n### Critical Metrics\n\n#### Compaction Activity\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total`** (Counter)\n  - Total compactions executed\n  - Healthy: Steadily increasing\n  - Alarm: No increase for >10 minutes with active writes\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_compactions_triggered_total`** (Counter)\n  - Total compaction attempts\n  - Healthy: Should exceed `compactions_total` (some are skipped)\n  - Warning: Triggered >> Executed (many failures)\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_compactions_failed_total`** (Counter)\n  - Failed compaction attempts\n  - Healthy: Should be 0 or very low\n  - **Red alert**: Any non-zero value indicates problems\n  - Note: Not incremented on context cancellation (shutdown)\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_compactions_skipped_total`** (Counter)\n  - Compactions skipped due to `--tsdb.auto-compaction-disabled`\n  - Normal when auto-compaction is disabled\n\n#### Compaction Performance\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds`** (Histogram)\n  - Time spent in compaction operations\n  - Healthy: p99 < 5 minutes, p99 < MinBlockDuration/2\n  - Warning: If duration approaches or exceeds `MinBlockDuration`, compactions are falling behind\n  - Critical: Log message at compact.go:1198 if duration > block time range\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_compaction_populating_block`** (Gauge, 0 or 1)\n  - Set to 1 during block writing, 0 when complete\n  - Healthy: Should be 0 most of the time\n  - Issue: Stuck at 1 indicates I/O problems or process hang\n\n#### Vertical Compaction (Overlapping Blocks)\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_vertical_compactions_total`** (Counter)\n  - Compactions of overlapping blocks\n  - Normal to increase if `EnableOverlappingCompaction=true`\n  - Indicates data arrived out-of-order\n\n#### Block and Storage Metrics\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_blocks_loaded`** (Gauge)\n  - Number of currently loaded blocks\n  - Healthy: Stable and not rapidly increasing\n  - Warning: Rapid growth suggests blocks are not being cleaned up\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_storage_blocks_bytes`** (Gauge)\n  - Total bytes used by all blocks\n  - Monitor against `prometheus_tsdb_retention_limit_bytes`\n  - If approaching limit, compaction may be blocked by retention\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_tombstone_cleanup_seconds`** (Histogram)\n  - Time to recompact blocks and remove tombstones\n  - High values indicate heavy delete operations\n\n#### Chunk Statistics (Level 1 Compactions Only)\n\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_compaction_chunk_size_bytes`**\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_compaction_chunk_samples`**\n- **`prometheus_tsdb_compaction_chunk_range_seconds`**\n\nThese indicate chunk quality; unusual distributions may suggest data quality issues.\n\n### Healthy Baseline\n\nFor a healthy Prometheus instance with 1-hour scrape of 10k series:\n\n```\nprometheus_tsdb_compactions_total: 50-100 per day\nprometheus_tsdb_compactions_triggered_total: 120-150 per day (some skipped/failed)\nprometheus_tsdb_compactions_failed_total: 0\nprometheus_tsdb_blocks_loaded: 30-50 blocks\nprometheus_tsdb_storage_blocks_bytes: 1-5 GiB (with default 15-day retention)\nprometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds: p99 < 2 minutes\n```\n\n### Alert Rules\n\n**PrometheusTSDBCompactionsFailing** (from prometheus-mixin):\n```\nincrease(prometheus_tsdb_compactions_failed_total{job=\"prometheus\"}[3h]) > 0\n```\n\nAdditional recommended alerts:\n\n```promql\n# Compaction falling behind\nincrease(prometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds_sum[5m]) /\n  increase(prometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds_count[5m]) > 300\n\n# Block accumulation\nincrease(prometheus_tsdb_blocks_loaded[30m]) > 5\n\n# Tombstone buildup\nprometheus_tsdb_blocks_loaded > 100\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. Failure Modes\n\n### Failure Mode 1: Disk Space Exhaustion During Compaction\n\n**Symptom:**\n- Compaction fails with error: \"no space left on device\"\n- Prometheus logs: `\"msg\"=\"compact blocks\" \"err\"=\"write block: ... : no such device\"`\n- Blocks stuck in `.tmp-for-creation` state\n- Metric: `prometheus_tsdb_compactions_failed_total` increments\n\n**Likely Cause:**\n- Insufficient disk space for compaction output (can require 2-3x the input block size during merge)\n- Retention limits not deleting old blocks\n- WAL not being truncated\n- Temporary block files not cleaned up from previous failed compactions\n\n**Diagnostic Steps:**\n\n1. Check disk usage:\n   ```bash\n   df -h /path/to/prometheus/data\n   ```\n\n2. Identify large blocks:\n   ```bash\n   du -sh /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/*/ | sort -h | tail -20\n   ```\n\n3. Check for orphaned tmp directories:\n   ```bash\n   find /path/to/prometheus/data -name \".tmp-for-*\" -type d\n   ls -la /path/to/prometheus/data/*.tmp/\n   ```\n\n4. Review retention settings:\n   ```bash\n   # Check configured retention\n   ps aux | grep prometheus | grep -E \"retention-size|storage.tsdb.retention\"\n   ```\n\n5. Check WAL size:\n   ```bash\n   du -sh /path/to/prometheus/data/wal/\n   ```\n\n6. Inspect Prometheus logs for which blocks failed:\n   ```bash\n   grep \"compact blocks\" prometheus.log | grep -i error | tail -20\n   ```\n\n**Code Reference:**\n- Compaction write: `tsdb/compact.go:606-717` (`LeveledCompactor.write()`)\n- Temporary directory cleanup: `tsdb/db.go:783-787`\n- Block deletion during failed compaction: `tsdb/compact.go:493-506`\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 2: Compaction Stuck or Not Progressing\n\n**Symptom:**\n- `prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total` and `prometheus_tsdb_compactions_triggered_total` stop increasing\n- `prometheus_tsdb_compaction_populating_block` stuck at 1\n- Query latency increases\n- Compaction duration increases steadily in logs\n- Blocks accumulate without being merged\n\n**Likely Cause:**\n- **I/O bottleneck**: Disk I/O saturation preventing block writes\n- **Memory pressure**: OOM killer or memory exhaustion preventing compaction progress\n- **Lock contention**: Compaction lock held by another operation\n- **Corrupted block**: Reading a corrupted source block blocks the entire compaction\n- **Slow disk**: NFS, storage array issues, or network-backed storage slowdowns\n- **Large blocks**: Attempting to compact excessively large blocks exceeds time/memory limits\n\n**Diagnostic Steps:**\n\n1. Check if Prometheus process is stuck:\n   ```bash\n   ps aux | grep prometheus\n   strace -p <pid> 2>&1 | head -20\n   ```\n\n2. Monitor system load and I/O:\n   ```bash\n   iostat -x 1 10\n   vmstat 1 10\n   top -p <prometheus_pid>\n   ```\n\n3. Check for OOM events:\n   ```bash\n   dmesg | grep -i \"oom\\|killed\\|memory\"\n   ```\n\n4. Examine compaction logs:\n   ```bash\n   tail -100 prometheus.log | grep -E \"compact|duration\"\n   ```\n\n5. Check block sizes:\n   ```bash\n   du -sh /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/*/ | sort -h | tail -5\n   # If largest block > 10GB, it may be too large to compact efficiently\n   ```\n\n6. Verify no blocks marked as failed:\n   ```bash\n   for block in /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/*/; do\n     grep -l '\"failed\":true' \"$block/meta.json\" 2>/dev/null && echo \"$block\"\n   done\n   ```\n\n**Code Reference:**\n- Compaction lock: `tsdb/db.go:1134` (`DB.cmtx`)\n- Duration warning: `tsdb/db.go:1197-1202` (logs if compaction exceeds `MinBlockDuration`)\n- Block population: `tsdb/compact.go:729-874` (`DefaultBlockPopulator.PopulateBlock()`)\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 3: Block Corruption\n\n**Symptom:**\n- Error on Prometheus startup: `\"corrupted block <ULID>: ...\"`\n- Index read errors: `\"open index reader for block ... : invalid checksum\"` or `\"corrupt index\"`\n- Query returns incomplete results from specific time ranges\n- Metric: `prometheus_tsdb_reloads_failures_total` increments\n- `prometheus_tsdb_blocks_loaded` drops suddenly\n\n**Likely Cause:**\n- **Incomplete block write**: Compaction crashed before fsync (especially on power loss)\n- **Metadata corruption**: Invalid `meta.json` or checksum mismatch\n- **Index file corruption**: Corruption in index file or chunks\n- **Filesystem inconsistency**: Unclean shutdown with corrupted filesystem\n- **Hardware failure**: Bit flip or disk sector error\n- **Unsafe snapshot**: Head chunks not properly re-encoded before compaction snapshot\n\n**Diagnostic Steps:**\n\n1. Identify corrupted blocks:\n   ```bash\n   # During startup, check Prometheus logs:\n   grep -i \"corrupted\" prometheus.log\n   ```\n\n2. Inspect block metadata:\n   ```bash\n   ls -la /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID>/\n   cat /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID>/meta.json | jq .\n   ```\n\n3. Check file integrity:\n   ```bash\n   cd /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID>/\n   # Verify required files exist\n   [ -f index ] && echo \"Index OK\" || echo \"MISSING: Index\"\n   [ -f chunks/000001 ] && echo \"Chunks OK\" || echo \"MISSING: Chunks\"\n   [ -f tombstones ] && echo \"Tombstones OK\" || echo \"MISSING: Tombstones\"\n   [ -f meta.json ] && echo \"Metadata OK\" || echo \"MISSING: Metadata\"\n   ```\n\n4. Check for incomplete creations:\n   ```bash\n   find /path/to/prometheus/data -name \".tmp-for-creation\" -type d\n   ```\n\n5. Validate block with promtool (if available):\n   ```bash\n   promtool tsdb check /path/to/prometheus/data\n   # or check individual block\n   promtool tsdb check /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID>/\n   ```\n\n**Code Reference:**\n- Block corruption detection on open: `tsdb/db.go:574-598` (`DBReadOnly.Blocks()`)\n- Meta file fsync: `tsdb/compact.go:702-703` (ensures metadata persisted)\n- WAL repair: `tsdb/db.go:918-933` (handles WAL corruption on startup)\n- Unsafe snapshot fix: `tsdb/compact.go:16` (CHANGELOG, re-encodes open chunks)\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 4: Out of Memory During Compaction\n\n**Symptom:**\n- Prometheus process killed by OOM killer: `dmesg | grep \"Killed process\"`\n- Compaction process exits without log message\n- `prometheus_tsdb_compactions_failed_total` increments (if processes restarts and detects failure)\n- Memory usage spikes during compaction before restart\n- Blocks may be left in `.tmp-for-creation` state\n\n**Likely Cause:**\n- **Large blocks being compacted**: Merging multiple large blocks (>5GB each) requires holding all data in memory\n- **High cardinality data**: Many unique series or labels increase in-memory symbol table\n- **Memory limit too low**: Container/pod memory limit insufficient for Prometheus + compaction\n- **Memory leaks**: Chunk pool not returning memory, builder allocations not freed\n- **Chunk pool exhaustion**: Too many chunks in flight, pool unable to recycle\n\n**Diagnostic Steps:**\n\n1. Check memory limit and usage:\n   ```bash\n   # Linux\n   free -h\n   cat /sys/fs/cgroup/memory.limit_in_bytes  # Cgroup limit\n   cat /sys/fs/cgroup/memory.usage_in_bytes  # Current usage\n   ```\n\n2. Monitor memory during compaction:\n   ```bash\n   watch -n 1 'ps aux | grep prometheus | grep -v grep'\n   # Note peak memory before OOM\n   ```\n\n3. Check for OOM events:\n   ```bash\n   dmesg | tail -30 | grep -i oom\n   docker logs <container> 2>&1 | grep -i oom  # For containers\n   ```\n\n4. Estimate block sizes:\n   ```bash\n   # If attempting to compact large blocks together:\n   du -sh /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/*/ | sort -h | tail -10\n   # Sum of largest blocks should fit in available memory\n   ```\n\n5. Check series cardinality:\n   ```bash\n   # Query Prometheus for cardinality (requires running instance)\n   curl -s http://localhost:9090/api/v1/label/__name__/values | jq 'length'\n   ```\n\n6. Inspect compaction plans:\n   ```bash\n   # Look at logs to see which blocks were selected for compaction\n   grep -E \"compact blocks|compaction plan\" prometheus.log | tail -20\n   ```\n\n**Code Reference:**\n- Block population allocates all data in memory: `tsdb/compact.go:729-874`\n- Symbol iteration: `tsdb/compact.go:803-810` (loads all symbols)\n- Chunk series merging: `tsdb/compact.go:812-823` (memory-intensive for large series sets)\n- Chunk pool exhaustion: `tsdb/compact.go:863-867` (returns chunks to pool)\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 5: WAL Corruption or Loss\n\n**Symptom:**\n- Prometheus startup error: `\"read WAL: ... error\" or \"read wal: ...\" or \"corrupted WAL\"`\n- Samples missing after a crash\n- Metric: `prometheus_tsdb_wal_reader_corruption_errors_total` increments\n- Compaction cannot complete (head block cannot persist)\n- `prometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds_count` stops increasing\n\n**Likely Cause:**\n- **Unclean shutdown**: Process killed or power loss during WAL write\n- **Corrupted WAL segment**: Disk error or incomplete write\n- **Disk full**: WAL write failed halfway through\n- **File system issue**: Metadata corruption or inode issues\n- **Concurrent WAL access**: Multiple instances writing to same TSDB directory\n\n**Diagnostic Steps:**\n\n1. Check WAL directory:\n   ```bash\n   ls -lh /path/to/prometheus/data/wal/\n   ```\n\n2. Check WAL segment integrity:\n   ```bash\n   # Prometheus will attempt to repair on startup; check logs:\n   grep -E \"WAL|wal\" prometheus.log | grep -i \"repair\\|error\" | head -20\n   ```\n\n3. Verify WAL repair status:\n   ```bash\n   grep \"Successfully repaired WAL\" prometheus.log  # Good sign\n   grep \"repair corrupted WAL\" prometheus.log       # Repair attempted\n   ```\n\n4. Check for WBL (write-behind log for out-of-order data):\n   ```bash\n   ls -lh /path/to/prometheus/data/wbl/ 2>/dev/null || echo \"No WBL\"\n   ```\n\n5. Monitor disk I/O during startup:\n   ```bash\n   # During restart, check:\n   iostat -x 1 | grep -E \"rrqm|wrqm|util\"\n   ```\n\n**Code Reference:**\n- WAL repair on startup: `tsdb/db.go:918-933` (automatic repair)\n- WAL truncation: `tsdb/db.go:1147-1150` (happens after successful compaction)\n- WBL (write-behind log) for OOO: `tsdb/db.go:858-863` (separate log for out-of-order samples)\n\n---\n\n## 4. Recovery Procedures\n\n### Procedure 1: Recover from Disk Space Exhaustion\n\n**Prerequisites:**\n- SSH/physical access to Prometheus instance\n- Sufficient disk space to add at least 10% more capacity or free up space\n\n**Steps:**\n\n1. **Stop Prometheus gracefully:**\n   ```bash\n   # Signal process to gracefully shutdown (gives it time to close files)\n   kill -TERM <prometheus_pid>\n   # Wait up to 30 seconds for graceful shutdown\n   sleep 30\n   if ps -p <prometheus_pid> > /dev/null; then\n     kill -9 <prometheus_pid>  # Force kill if still running\n   fi\n   ```\n\n2. **Clean up temporary block directories:**\n   ```bash\n   # Remove incomplete block creations (safe to delete)\n   find /path/to/prometheus/data -name \".tmp-for-*\" -type d -exec rm -rf {} + 2>/dev/null || true\n   ls -la /path/to/prometheus/data/*.tmp 2>/dev/null | xargs rm -rf || true\n   ```\n\n3. **Check WAL truncation:**\n   ```bash\n   # WAL can be large; compress if needed\n   du -sh /path/to/prometheus/data/wal/\n   # Note: Don't delete WAL; let Prometheus handle it on restart\n   ```\n\n4. **Verify block consistency:**\n   ```bash\n   # List all blocks\n   ls /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/\n\n   # Check for blocks with failed compaction flag\n   for block in /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/*/; do\n     if grep -q '\"failed\":true' \"$block/meta.json\" 2>/dev/null; then\n       echo \"Failed block: $block\"\n     fi\n   done\n   ```\n\n5. **Optional: Delete oldest blocks if still out of space**\n   ```bash\n   # Only if disk is still critically low\n   # List blocks by date (ULID timestamp)\n   ls -la /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/ | sort -k6\n\n   # Delete oldest 2-3 blocks (they're the smallest)\n   # WARNING: This loses data outside retention!\n   rm -rf /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<oldest_ULID>\n   ```\n\n6. **Restart Prometheus:**\n   ```bash\n   # Restart with monitoring\n   systemctl start prometheus  # or docker run, kubectl apply, etc.\n\n   # Verify startup\n   sleep 10\n   curl -s http://localhost:9090/-/healthy\n   ```\n\n7. **Monitor recovery:**\n   ```bash\n   # Watch for compaction to resume\n   watch 'curl -s http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total | jq'\n\n   # Check error logs\n   tail -f prometheus.log | grep -E \"compact|error|warn\"\n   ```\n\n8. **Verify disk recovery:**\n   ```bash\n   # After 30 minutes, check if disk usage decreasing\n   watch -n 60 'du -sh /path/to/prometheus/data; df -h /path/to/prometheus/data'\n   ```\n\n**Expected Outcome:**\n- `prometheus_tsdb_compactions_failed_total` stays stable (no new failures)\n- `prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total` resumes increasing\n- Disk usage stabilizes and then decreases as old blocks are deleted by retention\n\n---\n\n### Procedure 2: Recover from Stuck Compaction\n\n**Prerequisites:**\n- Prometheus instance is running but compaction not progressing\n- At least 5 minutes of observation confirming no progress\n\n**Steps:**\n\n1. **Verify compaction is truly stuck:**\n   ```bash\n   # Check if compaction counter increasing\n   curl -s http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=rate(prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total[5m]) | jq '.data.result[0].value[1]'\n   # Should be > 0 if healthy\n\n   # If query returns \"null\" or \"0\", compaction is likely stuck\n   ```\n\n2. **Check system resources:**\n   ```bash\n   # CPU usage\n   top -p <prometheus_pid> -b -n 1 | tail -5\n\n   # Disk I/O\n   iostat -x 1 5 | tail -10\n\n   # Memory\n   ps aux | grep prometheus | grep -v grep | awk '{print $6 \" KB\"}'\n   ```\n\n3. **Identify the blocked block:**\n   ```bash\n   # Find what compaction is processing\n   lsof -p <prometheus_pid> | grep /blocks/ | head -10\n   # Look for which block directory is open\n\n   # Check metadata of candidates\n   for block in /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/*/; do\n     size=$(du -sh \"$block\" | cut -f1)\n     echo \"$block: $size\"\n   done | sort -h -k3 | tail -5\n   ```\n\n4. **Check logs for last compaction attempt:**\n   ```bash\n   tail -200 prometheus.log | grep -E \"compact|error|duration\" | tail -20\n   ```\n\n5. **Gracefully restart Prometheus:**\n   ```bash\n   # Trigger graceful shutdown\n   systemctl stop prometheus  # or equivalent\n\n   # Wait for shutdown\n   sleep 30\n   ```\n\n6. **Check for corrupted source block:**\n   ```bash\n   # If blocks are suspected corrupted, validate with promtool\n   promtool tsdb check /path/to/prometheus/data 2>&1 | head -50\n   # Look for \"corrupted\" errors\n   ```\n\n7. **Restart Prometheus:**\n   ```bash\n   systemctl start prometheus\n   sleep 15\n   curl -s http://localhost:9090/-/healthy\n   ```\n\n8. **Monitor for issue recurrence:**\n   ```bash\n   # Watch compaction duration\n   watch -n 10 'curl -s \"http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=rate(prometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds_sum[5m])/rate(prometheus_tsdb_compaction_duration_seconds_count[5m])\" | jq \".data.result[0].value[1]\" 2>/dev/null || echo \"unavailable\"'\n\n   # Should see compactions resuming within 1-2 minutes\n   ```\n\n**Expected Outcome:**\n- `prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total` resumes increasing after restart\n- Compaction duration returns to normal (<5 minutes)\n- No \"stuck\" symptoms after 10 minutes of monitoring\n\n---\n\n### Procedure 3: Recover from Block Corruption\n\n**Prerequisites:**\n- Prometheus cannot start or logs show `\"corrupted block\"` error\n- Identify the corrupted block ULID from logs\n\n**Steps:**\n\n1. **Identify corrupted blocks:**\n   ```bash\n   # Try to start Prometheus and capture error\n   prometheus --config.file=/etc/prometheus/prometheus.yml 2>&1 | grep -i \"corrupted\"\n   # Note the ULID in the error\n\n   # Or check all blocks:\n   for block in /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/*/; do\n     if ! promtool tsdb check \"$block\" &>/dev/null; then\n       echo \"Corrupted: $block\"\n     fi\n   done\n   ```\n\n2. **Determine block importance:**\n   ```bash\n   # Get block time range\n   cat /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID>/meta.json | jq '{minTime: .minTime, maxTime: .maxTime}'\n\n   # Convert timestamps (milliseconds since epoch)\n   python3 -c \"import datetime; print(datetime.datetime.fromtimestamp(1234567890 / 1000))\"\n   ```\n\n3. **Check if block has children (i.e., was compacted):**\n   ```bash\n   # If this block is parent of others, don't delete it\n   grep -r '<ULID>' /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/*/meta.json | grep \"sources\" | head -10\n   # If no results, block is safe to delete\n   ```\n\n4. **Option A: Delete corrupted block (data loss for time range)**\n   ```bash\n   # This is safe if block has been replaced by newer compacted blocks\n   rm -rf /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID>\n\n   # Verify deletion\n   ls /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID> 2>/dev/null || echo \"Block deleted\"\n   ```\n\n5. **Option B: Attempt repair with promtool (experimental)**\n   ```bash\n   # First backup the block\n   cp -r /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID> /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID>.backup\n\n   # Attempt repair (not always successful)\n   promtool tsdb repair /path/to/prometheus/data 2>&1\n\n   # Check if fixed\n   promtool tsdb check /path/to/prometheus/data/blocks/<ULID> 2>&1\n   ```\n\n6. **Restart Prometheus:**\n   ```bash\n   prometheus --config.file=/etc/prometheus/prometheus.yml &\n   sleep 10\n   curl -s http://localhost:9090/-/healthy\n   ```\n\n7. **Verify recovery:**\n   ```bash\n   # Check that Prometheus is queryable\n   curl -s 'http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=up' | jq '.status'\n   # Should return \"success\"\n\n   # Verify block loading\n   curl -s 'http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=prometheus_tsdb_blocks_loaded' | jq '.data.result[0].value[1]'\n   ```\n\n**Expected Outcome:**\n- Prometheus starts without corruption errors\n- Metrics queryable from remaining blocks\n- Data loss limited to corrupted block's time range\n\n**Note:** If multiple blocks are corrupted, consider full database rebuild from backups.\n\n---\n\n### Procedure 4: Recover from OOM During Compaction\n\n**Prerequisites:**\n- Prometheus was killed by OOM killer\n- Available memory or pod memory limit can be increased\n- Database backups available (optional but recommended)\n\n**Steps:**\n\n1. **Verify OOM occurred:**\n   ```bash\n   dmesg | tail -20 | grep -i \"oom\\|killed\"\n   # Should show: \"Killed process <pid> (prometheus)\"\n   ```\n\n2. **Increase memory limit (if container/pod):**\n   ```bash\n   # Docker\n   docker update --memory 8g <container_id>\n\n   # Kubernetes\n   kubectl set resources deployment prometheus --limits=memory=8G\n\n   # Systemd service: edit /etc/systemd/system/prometheus.service\n   # Add: MemoryLimit=8G\n   systemctl daemon-reload\n   ```\n\n3. **Clean up incomplete blocks:**\n   ```bash\n   # Remove temporary block creations\n   find /path/to/prometheus/data -name \".tmp-for-*\" -type d -exec rm -rf {} + 2>/dev/null || true\n   ```\n\n4. **Reduce block compaction size (optional, advanced):**\n   ```bash\n   # Edit Prometheus config to use smaller blocks\n   # This prevents very large merges that cause OOM\n\n   # Add to prometheus.yml (restart required):\n   # storage:\n   #   tsdb:\n   #     min-block-duration: 1h\n   #     max-block-duration: 1h  # Prevent large merges\n   ```\n\n5. **Restart Prometheus:**\n   ```bash\n   systemctl start prometheus\n   # or docker run with new memory limit\n   docker run --memory 8g ... prometheus\n\n   sleep 15\n   curl -s http://localhost:9090/-/healthy\n   ```\n\n6. **Monitor memory and compaction:**\n   ```bash\n   # Watch memory during first compaction\n   watch -n 5 'ps aux | grep prometheus | grep -v grep | awk \"{print \\$6 \\\" KB\\\"}\"'\n\n   # In another terminal, monitor compaction\n   watch -n 5 'curl -s \"http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total\" | jq \".data.result[0].value[1]\" 2>/dev/null || echo \"loading\"'\n   ```\n\n7. **Verify stable operation:**\n   ```bash\n   # After 1 hour of operation, check for OOM recurrence\n   dmesg | tail -10 | grep -i \"oom\" || echo \"No new OOM events\"\n\n   # Check compaction metrics\n   curl -s 'http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=prometheus_tsdb_compactions_failed_total' | jq '.data.result[0].value[1]'\n   # Should be \"0\"\n   ```\n\n**Expected Outcome:**\n- Prometheus runs without OOM restarts\n- Memory usage stabilizes below limit during compaction\n- Compactions complete successfully\n\n**Long-term mitigation:**\n- Reduce series cardinality (drop unnecessary labels/series)\n- Increase retention interval or use size-based retention\n- Use query optimization to reduce query memory footprint\n\n---\n\n### Procedure 5: Recover from WAL Corruption\n\n**Prerequisites:**\n- Prometheus fails to start with WAL errors\n- WAL corruption is unrecoverable or too severe to repair\n\n**Steps:**\n\n1. **Verify WAL is the issue:**\n   ```bash\n   # Try to start Prometheus\n   prometheus --config.file=/etc/prometheus/prometheus.yml 2>&1 | grep -i \"wal\\|wbl\"\n\n   # Should see error like:\n   # \"Encountered WAL read error, attempting repair\"\n   # \"repair corrupted WAL: ...\"\n   ```\n\n2. **Let Prometheus attempt auto-repair:**\n   ```bash\n   # The code in tsdb/db.go:918-933 automatically repairs WAL\n   # Just restart Prometheus; it will try to fix issues\n   prometheus --config.file=/etc/prometheus/prometheus.yml &\n   sleep 30\n   jobs\n   # If process is running, repair succeeded\n   ```\n\n3. **Check repair status:**\n   ```bash\n   # Look for success message\n   grep \"Successfully repaired\" prometheus.log\n   # If found, WAL was fixed; Prometheus should be running\n\n   curl -s http://localhost:9090/-/healthy\n   ```\n\n4. **If auto-repair fails, manually reset WAL:**\n   ```bash\n   # WARNING: This loses data in the WAL (typically <2 hours of data)\n\n   # Stop Prometheus\n   kill -9 <prometheus_pid>\n\n   # Backup corrupted WAL\n   mv /path/to/prometheus/data/wal /path/to/prometheus/data/wal.corrupted\n   mkdir -p /path/to/prometheus/data/wal\n\n   # Backup WBL (write-behind log) if it exists\n   if [ -d /path/to/prometheus/data/wbl ]; then\n     mv /path/to/prometheus/data/wbl /path/to/prometheus/data/wbl.corrupted\n   fi\n   ```\n\n5. **Restart Prometheus with empty WAL:**\n   ```bash\n   prometheus --config.file=/etc/prometheus/prometheus.yml &\n   sleep 10\n   curl -s http://localhost:9090/-/healthy\n\n   # Should be running with new WAL\n   ls -la /path/to/prometheus/data/wal/\n   ```\n\n6. **Verify data recovery:**\n   ```bash\n   # Check how much data was lost\n   curl -s 'http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=prometheus_tsdb_blocks_loaded' | jq '.data.result[0].value[1]'\n   # Should still show blocks from persisted storage\n\n   # Query for time range to see what data remains\n   curl -s 'http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query_range?query=up&start=...&end=...&step=...' | jq '.data'\n   ```\n\n7. **Monitor compaction after WAL reset:**\n   ```bash\n   # New compaction may be triggered to persist head data\n   tail -f prometheus.log | grep -E \"compact|wal\"\n\n   # Check that compactions complete successfully\n   watch -n 30 'curl -s http://localhost:9090/api/v1/query?query=rate(prometheus_tsdb_compactions_total[5m]) | jq \".data.result[0].value[1]\"'\n   ```\n\n**Expected Outcome:**\n- Prometheus starts and serves queries\n- Data loss limited to samples in lost WAL (typically < 2 hours)\n- Blocks on disk are preserved\n- New WAL created for future samples\n\n**Note:** If WAL corruption is recurring, check for hardware issues (disk errors, memory corruption) or filesystem problems.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Attempts repair on startup\n  - WAL repair: line 929 – `wal.Repair(initErr)`\n  - WBL repair: line 923 – `wbl.Repair(e.err)`\n- **WAL truncation after compaction**: `tsdb/db.go:1147-1150` – Cleans WAL after successful compaction\n- **Repair code**: `tsdb/repair.go:30-100` – Index version repair (legacy)\n\n### Monitoring Metrics Reference\n\n**From `tsdb/compact.go`:**\n- Line 104:
